Question: A computer routine was developed to generate two numbers (x,y) the first being a random number between 0 and 100 inclusive, and the second being less than or equal to the square root of the first. Each of the following pair satisfies the routine except
Choices:
  A: (99,10)
  B: (85,9)
  C: (50,7)
  D: (1,1)
  E: (1,0)
Response 0:
Thought:
  If the first number is 0, the second number can only be 0 as well.
  If the first number is 1, the second number can only be 1 as well.
  For all other cases, the second number can be any integer between 0 and the square root of the first number inclusive.
  Therefore, the only pair that does not satisfy the routine is (1,0) because the second number should be less than or equal to the square root of the first number, which is 1.
Action: Answer("E")

  For pair (85, 9) the second number is less than or equal to the square root of the first number, so it satisfies the routine.

  For pair (1, 0) the second number is equal to the square root of the first number, which is not less than or equal to the first number. Therefore, it does not satisfy the routine.
  The answer is E: (1,0)

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If 75 percent of the employees of a certain company take a winter vacation, 40 percent take a winter and a summer vacation, and 20 percent take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, what Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation?
Choices:
  A: 5%
  B: 15%
  C: 25%
  D: 35%
  E: 45%
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume there are 100 employees in the company.
  75% of the employees take a winter vacation, so 75 employees take a winter vacation and 25 employees do not take a winter vacation.
  40% of the employees take a winter and a summer vacation, so 40 employees take a winter and a summer vacation.
  20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, so 20 employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation and 80 employees take at least one of the two vacations.
  We want to find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  Let x be the number of employees who take only a summer vacation. Then, the total number of employees who take a summer vacation is (x + 40).
  The total number of employees who take at least one of the two vacations is 80. 
  Hence, (x + 40 + 75) - 100 = (x + 15) is the number of employees who take both a winter AND a summer vacation.
  Therefore, the number of employees who take only a summer vacation is (x + 40) - (x + 15) = 25.
  Therefore, the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation = 25 / 100 * 100 = 25%.
  The answer is C: 25%.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let x be the number of employees.
75% of the employees take a winter vacation. Hence, 25% of the employees do not take a winter vacation.
20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation. Hence, 80% of the employees take at least one vacation.
40% of the employees take both winter and summer vacations. Hence, 40% of the employees take a summer vacation (including those who also take a winter vacation).
Thus, the Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is:
Q% = (percentage of employees who take a summer vacation) - (percentage of employees who take both summer and winter vacations)
Q% = (40% of x) - (40% of x - 25% of x)
Q% = 25% of x
Therefore, the answer is C: 25%. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We can use Venn Diagrams to represent this information.
  Let's assume that there are a total of 100 employees in the company.
  If 75% of the employees take a winter vacation, then 25% of the employees do not take a winter vacation.
  If 40% of the employees take a winter and a summer vacation, then this group is a subset of the winter vacation group. 
  Let's represent this with the following Venn Diagram:
  
  [image source: https://i.imgur.com/ZJ3uG5m.png]
  
  We know that 20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation. So, the remaining 80% of the employees must fall into at least one of the two vacation categories. 
  To find out what Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation, we need to find the value of Q.
  Let's assume that the percentage of employees who take only a summer vacation is Q1.
  Therefore, the percentage of employees who take both winter and summer vacations is 40% - Q1.
  The percentage of employees who take only a winter vacation is (25% - 40% + Q1) = (Q1 - 15%).
  The percentage of employees who take both winter and summer vacations is 40% - Q1.
  The percentage of employees who take only a summer vacation is (Q - Q1).
  We know that the percentage of employees who take no vacation is 20%.
  Therefore, the percentage of employees who take at least one vacation is 100% - 20% = 80%.
  Using this information, we can create the following equation:
  Q1 + (Q1 - 15%) + (Q - Q1) + (40% - Q1) = 80%
  Solving for Q1, we get:
  Q1 = 15%
  Therefore, the percentage of employees who take only a summer vacation is Q - Q1 = Q - 15%
  Since we don't know the value of Q, we cannot determine the exact percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  However, we do know that the percentage must be less than or equal to 15%, since Q1 is 15%.
  Therefore, the best answer is A: 5%.

Thought:
  We know that:
  75% of the employees take a winter vacation.
  40% of the employees take a winter and a summer vacation.
  20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation.
  We want to find the percentage of employees that take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  Let's assume that there are 100 employees in total, so:
  75 employees take a winter vacation.
  40 employees take both winter and summer vacations.
  20 employees take neither vacation.
  That leaves 100 - 75 - 20 = 5 employees who don't take a winter vacation.
  We want to find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  Let's call that percentage Q.
  We know that 40% of employees take both winter and summer vacations.
  That means that the remaining summer vacationers are 100% - 40% = 60% of the employees.
  We also know that 5 employees don't take a winter vacation.
  Of those 5 employees, we know that none take both winter and summer vacations.
  Therefore, Q% = (number of employees taking only summer vacation / total number of employees) x 100%
  Q% = (number of employees taking summer vacation but not winter vacation / total number of employees) x 100%
  Q% = (60% - 0% - Q% / 100% - 20%) x 100%
  Q% = (60% - Q% / 80%) x 100%
  Q% = (48 - Q%) x 5/4
  Q% = 240/9
  Q% = 26.67%
  Therefore, the answer is C: 25%.

  Then, 75% of N employees take a winter vacation. This means 25% of N employees do not take a winter vacation.
  Also, 20% of N employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation. This means 80% of N employees take either a winter or a summer vacation or both.

  Therefore, (25 - 53.33)% = -28.33% of employees take only a winter vacation.
  Let y% of employees take only a summer vacation. Then, (y + x)% of employees take either a summer or a winter vacation but not both.
  We know that 80% of the employees take either a summer or a winter vacation or both, so (y + x)% = 80% - 20% = 60%.
  Therefore, y% = (60% - x%).
  We need to find Q% of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation. This is the same as y% - x%.
  Therefore, Q% = (60% - x%) - x% = 60% - 2x%.
  We need to find x% to calculate Q%. 
  We know that (25 - 53.33)% = -28.33% of employees take only a winter vacation. This is the same as (75% - 53.33%) = 21.67% of employees taking only a summer vacation.
  Therefore, (y + x)% = 60% - 21.67% = 38.33%.
  Solving for x%, we get x% = 18.33%.
  Therefore, Q% = 60% - 2x% = 60% - 36.66% = 23.34%.
  The closest answer is C: 25%.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 3 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight of its vertices are on the sphere. What is the diameter of the sphere?
Choices:
  A:  13.3542
  B:  15.8113
  C:  18.3451
  D:  19.5667
  E:  20.8888
Response 0:
Thought:
  A rectangular solid is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight vertices are on the sphere.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is the diameter of the sphere.
  We can find the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid by using the Pythagorean theorem.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is the square root of the sum of the squares of its three dimensions.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is the square root of (3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) which is the square root of 250.
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the square root of 250 times 2.
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is approximately 15.8113.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The diagonal of one face of the rectangular solid is the diameter of the sphere.
  Using Pythagorean theorem, the diagonal of the rectangular solid is sqrt(3^2+4^2+15^2) = sqrt(250).
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is sqrt(250) times 2.
  To simplify, sqrt(250) can be written as 5*sqrt(10).
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is 2 * 5 * sqrt(10) = 10*sqrt(10).
  The answer is E: 20.8888.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Peter wants to find 10 additional people to form a scavenger hunt team with him. If he has 10 friends who would like to participate, how many choices does he have for forming his team?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 1
  C: 2
  D: 3
  E: 4
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Peter has 10 friends who would like to participate.
  Peter is selecting 10 people from the 10 friends to form a team.
  The number of ways to choose r items from n items is given by the formula nCr, where n is the number of items and r is the number of items to choose.
  In this case, n = 10 (Peter's friends) and r = 10 (number of people in the team).
  Therefore, the number of choices Peter has for forming his team is 10C10 = 1.
  The answer is B: 1.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Peter has 10 friends to choose from.
  He wants to find 10 additional people, which means he needs to choose 10 people from the remaining friends.
  This is a combination problem where order doesn't matter and repetition isn't allowed.
  The formula for combination is nCr = n! / (r! * (n - r)!), where n is the total number of options, and r is the number of choices.
  In this case, n = 10 and r = 10.
  10C10 = 10! / (10! * 0!) = 1
  Therefore, Peter only has 1 choice for forming his team.
  The answer is B: 1.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Peter has 10 friends who would like to participate.
  He needs to pick 10 people from those friends to form a team.
  The order in which he picks people doesn't matter.
  This is a combination problem.
  The number of combinations of n objects taken k at a time is given by the formula C(n,k) = n! / (k!(n-k)!).
  Peter has 10 friends to choose from, and he needs to pick 10 of them.
  C(10,10) = 10! / (10!(10-10)!) = 1.
  Therefore, Peter has only 1 choice for forming his team.
Action: Answer("B")

  The order in which he chooses the people for his team does not matter.
  This is a combination problem because we are selecting a group of people from a larger group.
  The formula for combinations is n choose r = n! / (r! * (n-r)!), where n is the total number of items and r is the number of items being chosen.
  In this case, n = 10 (Peter's friends) and r = 10 (the number of people he wants on his team).
  Therefore, the number of choices Peter has for forming his team is 10 choose 10 = 1.
  The answer is B: 1.

The number of possible ways to choose a combination of 10 people from a group of 10 friends is given by the formula: 10! / (10-10)!10!
Simplifying the formula, we get 10! / 0!10!
0! is equal to 1, so we can simplify further to get 10! / 10!
10! / 10! = 1
Therefore, Peter has only one choice for forming his team.
The answer is B: 1.

  A: 8
  B: 10
  C: 12
  D: 15
  E: 19
Response 0:
Thought:
To find out how many helpers are required:
- We need to determine how many large cakes and how many small cakes can be made in 3 hours.
- We can then use this information to determine how many helpers are required.

Calculation:
In 1 hour, each helper can make either:
- 2 large cakes or
- 35 small cakes

So, in 3 hours, each helper can make:
- 2 x 3 = 6 large cakes or
- 35 x 3 = 105 small cakes

To make 20 large cakes, we need:
- 20 / 6 = 3.33 (round up to 4) helpers to make large cakes

To make 700 small cakes, we need:
- 700 / 105 = 6.67 (round up to 7) helpers to make small cakes

The maximum number of helpers required is 7 because we need more helpers to make small cakes than large cakes.

Answer:
Therefore, the answer is B: 10.

  B: 39 seconds
  C: 20 seconds
  D: 33 seconds

  We can use the formula: time = distance / speed.
  We need to convert the speed from miles per hour to miles per second.
  1 hour = 3600 seconds. Therefore, 120 miles per hour = 120/3600 miles per second.
  So, speed = 1/30 miles per second.
  time = distance / speed = 1 / (1/30) = 30 seconds.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 33 seconds.

Question: An electric pole, 14 metres high, casts a shadow of 10 metres. Find the height of a tree that casts a shadow of 15 metres under similar conditions.

  B: 22
  C: 20

  From the given information, we can form a proportion as follows:
  (height of electric pole) : (length of shadow of electric pole) = (height of tree) : (length of shadow of tree)
  14 : 10 = h : 15
  Solving for h, we get:
  h = (14 x 15) / 10
  h = 21
  Therefore, the height of the tree is 21 meters.
  The answer is A: 21.

  The height to shadow ratio of the electric pole is 14/10 = 1.4
  Let x be the height of the tree that casts a shadow of 15 metres.
  The height to shadow ratio of the tree is x/15.
  Since the conditions are similar, the height to shadow ratios of the pole and the tree are equal.
  Therefore, we can set up an equation as follows: 1.4 = x/15
  Solving for x, we get x = 21.
  Therefore, the height of the tree is 21 metres.

  C: 1,876
  D: 1,872
  E: 1,800

  Therefore, the selling price after the discount would be (x - 0.2x) = 0.8x.
  Karan wants to make a 20% profit. Therefore, his profit would be 0.2 * 1200 = 240.
  His total revenue would be the selling price after the discount (0.8x) plus his profit (240).
  Thus, the equation would be 0.8x + 240 = cost price + profit
  We know that the cost price is Rs. 1200.
  Substituting this in the equation, we get 0.8x + 240 = 1200 + 240.
  Solving the equation, we get 0.8x = 1200, which means x = 1500.
  Therefore, the selling price of the sewing machine should be Rs. 1500.

Question: John would make the 3-letter codes with diffenrent 5 vowels and 20 consonants with the condition that the middle letter must be vowel and the first letter and the third letter must be different from each other and are both consonant. How many different codes can be made?
Choices:
  A: 1,980
  B: 2,020
  C: 2,100
  D: 2,200
  E: 1,900
Response 0:
Thought:
  The middle letter must be vowel which means there are 5 choices for the middle letter.
  The first and third letters must be different from each other and must be consonants. Thus, there are 20 choices for the first letter and 19 choices for the third letter. (One less than 20 because the first and third letters must be different from each other.)
  Therefore, the number of different codes that can be made is 5 x 20 x 19 = 1,900.
  The answer is E: 1,900.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:

  There are 20 consonants that can be used for the first and third letters.

  There are P(20, 2) = 380 ways to do this.
  For each choice of consonants, there are 5 x 20 = 100 ways to choose the vowels for the code.
  Therefore, the total number of different codes that can be made is 380 x 100 = 38,000.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 11 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: At a certain factory, 10 percent of the staplers produced on Monday were defective and 2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, what was the number of staplers produced that day?
Choices:
  A: 4,000
  B: 4,200
  C: 4,500
  D: 4,800
  E: 5,000
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's say that x is the total number of staplers produced on Monday. 
10% of the staplers were defective, so 90% of the staplers were non-defective. 
2% of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake, so 98% of the non-defective staplers were not rejected.
We know that 72 non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. 
We can set up an equation using the above information:
0.98(0.9x) = x - 72 (the number of non-defective staplers not rejected = total staplers minus defective staplers minus non-defective staplers rejected)
Solving for x:
0.882x = x - 72
0.118x = 72
x = 610.17
The number of staplers produced cannot be a decimal, so we have to round up to the nearest integer, which is 611.
Therefore, the number of staplers produced that day was 611.
The answer is not one of the given choices.
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's assume that the number of staplers produced is x. 
10% of the staplers produced on Monday were defective, so 90% of the staplers produced on Monday were non-defective. 
2% of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake
If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, then we can set up the equation as follows: 
0.02 * 0.9 * x = 72
Solving the equation: 
0.018 * x = 72
x = 4000
Therefore, the number of staplers produced that day is 4000.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 12 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D. If 3 men drop out how much more will each have to contribute towards the purchase of the gift?
Choices:
  A: D/(M-3)
  B: MD/3
  C: M/(D-3)
  D: 3D/(M2-3M)
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  Initially, each of the M men would have to contribute D/M Rs towards the purchase of the gift.
  If 3 men drop out, then there are M-3 men left who have to contribute towards the purchase of the gift.
  Since the total amount to be contributed is still D, the new contribution per person would be D/(M-3).
  The question asks how much more each person has to contribute compared to the original contribution, which is (D/(M-3)) - (D/M).
  Simplifying this expression, we get (DM/(M-3)) - (DM/M) = 3D/(M(M-3)).
  Therefore, the answer is D: 3D/(M^2-3M).
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Initially, M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D.
  So, the amount that each person contributes is D/M.
  When 3 men drop out, the number of men left is (M-3).
  The total amount to be paid, however, remains the same and is still D.
  Therefore, each person now has to contribute D/(M-3).
  Therefore, the answer is A: D/(M-3).
Action: Answer("A")

Action: Answer("A")
Response 6:
Thought:
  Initially, M men agreed to purchase a gift for Rs. D.
  Let's assume each man would have contributed x amount for the gift.
  Hence, the total amount collected would have been Mx.
  But now, only (M-3) men are purchasing the gift.
  So, the total amount collected would be (M-3)y (where y is the new contribution by each man)
  Since the gift amount remains the same, we can equate the two expressions:
  Mx = (M-3)y
  y = (Mx)/(M-3)
  Each person has to contribute an additional amount than before, which is (y-x)
  substituting y in terms of x, we get:
  (y-x) = (Mx)/(M-3) - x
  simplifying the above expression, we get:
  (y-x) = (3x)/(M-3)
  (y-x) = 3x(M2-3M)
  Therefore, each person has to contribute 3x/(M-3) more towards the purchase of the gift.
  Hence, the answer is D: 3D/(M2-3M).

Topic: Math
Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs?
Choices:
  A: 0.5
  B: 0.6
  C: 0.7
  D: 0.8
  E: 0.9
Response 0:
Thought:
  If A and B are independent, then P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  If at least one of A or B occurs, then P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  We are given that P(A) = 0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96.
  We can solve for P(B) using the formula P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  First, we rearrange the formula to solve for P(A and B): P(A and B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A or B).
  Then, we substitute in the known values: P(A and B) = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B)) = 0.6 + 0.4P(B).
  Finally, we solve for P(B): P(B) = (P(A and B) - 0.6) / 0.4.
  We know that A and B are independent, so P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B) = 0.6 * P(B).
  Substituting in this expression for P(A and B), we get P(B) = (0.6 * P(B) - 0.6) / 0.4 = 1.5 * P(B) - 1.5.
  Solving for P(B), we get P(B) = 0.7.
  Therefore, the probability that event B occurs is 0.7.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought: 
  P(A) = 0.6

  Since A and B are independent, P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B)

  Substitute known values and solve for P(B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6 * P(B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4 * P(B)
  0.36 = 0.4 * P(B)

Question: Two balls A and B rotate along a circular track. Ball A makes 2 full rotations in 26 minutes. Ball B makes 5 full rotation in 35 minutes. If they start rotating now from the same point, when will they be at the same starting point again?
Choices:
  A: 1 hour and 31 minutes
  B: 2 hour and 31 minutes
  C: 3 hour and 31 minutes
  D: 4 hour and 31 minutes
  E: 5 hour and 31 minutes
Response 0:
Thought:
  The time taken for ball A to complete 1 full rotation is 26/2 = 13 minutes.
  The time taken for ball B to complete 1 full rotation is 35/5 = 7 minutes.
  Let's assume they start at 12:00 pm. 
  After 1 hour, Ball A would have completed 4 full rotations and Ball B would have completed 12 full rotations. They will meet after LCM(4,12) rotations.
  LCM(4,12) = 12 minutes.
  Therefore, they will be at the same starting point again after 12 minutes, which is at 12:12 pm.
  The answer is not among the choices given.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The time required for a ball to make one full rotation is the reciprocal of its rotational speed.
  The rotational speed of ball A is 2 rotations per 26 minutes, which is 1 rotation per 13 minute.
  The rotational speed of ball B is 5 rotations per 35 minutes, which is 1 rotation per 7 minutes.
  We need to find the smallest positive integer n such that ball A will have completed n rotations when ball B completes n+1 rotations.
  If n is the number of rotations of ball A, then ball A will have completed n rotations in n x 13 minutes.
  If n+1 is the number of rotations of ball B, then ball B will have complete n+1 rotations in (n+1) x 7 minutes.
  The two balls will be at the same starting point again when ball A and ball B complete the same number of rotations.
  Therefore, we need to find n such that n x 13 = (n+1) x 7.
  Solving for n, we get n = 13/6, which is approximately 2.17.
  Since n must be a positive integer, we round up to n = 3.
  Therefore, the two balls will be at the same starting point again after 3 x 13 = 39 minutes.
  The answer is A: 1 hour and 31 minutes since 39 minutes is equal to 0 hour and 39 minutes.

Question: A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be :
Choices:
  A: 12 metre
  B: 12.5 metre
  C: 13.5 metre
  D: 14 metre
  E: 15 metre
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's use the concept of similar triangles.
  The ratio of the height of the flagstaff to the length of its shadow is equal to the ratio of the height of the building to the length of its shadow.
  Let x be the height of the building.
  We can set up a proportion: 17.5/40.25 = x/28.75
  Solving for x: x = 12.5
  Therefore, the height of the building is 12.5 meters.
  The answer is B: 12.5 meter.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:

  The length of the shadow of the flagstaff is 17.5 meters.
  The length of the shadow of the building is 28.75 meters.

  we can say that 17.5 / 40.25 = h / 28.75
  Solving for 'h', we get h = (17.5 x 28.75) / 40.25 = 12.5 meters.
  Therefore, the height of the building is 12.5 meters.

Question: Suppose you want to arrange your English, Hindi, Mathematics, History, Geography and Science books on a shelf. In how many ways can you do it ?
Choices:
  A: 520
  B: 720
  C: 920
  D: None
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Thought:
  We have 6 books that can be arranged in any order on a shelf.
  The first book can be any of the 6 books.
  The second book can be any of the remaining 5 books.
  This continues until all 6 books are on the shelf.
  Therefore, the total number of ways the books can be arranged is 6 x 5 x 4 x 3 x 2 x 1 = 720.
  The answer is B: 720.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Since there are 6 different books, we can arrange them in 6! ways (6 factorial).
  6! = 6 x 5 x 4 x 3 x 2 x 1 = 720
  Therefore, the answer is B: 720.
Action: Answer("B")

Thought:

  This is a permutation problem, because order matters.
  The number of ways to arrange n distinct objects is n factorial (n!).
  Therefore, the number of ways to arrange 6 books is 6! = 720.
  The answer is B: 720.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 20 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers?
Choices:
  A: (zy – 2x)/z
  B: (zy – 2)/z
  C: (zx – y)/(z – 2)
  D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2)
  E: (zy – x)/(z + 2)
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the highest score is H and the lowest score is L.
  We know that (H + L)/2 = x  --- equation 1
  We also know that the average of the entire class is y, therefore (sum of all scores) / z = y
  Let's assume that the sum of all scores is S.
  Therefore, S/z = y   --- equation 2
  We need to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers.
  Let's assume that the sum of the scores excluding the highest and lowest scorers is E.
  We know that E/(z-2) is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers.
  We can express E in terms of S, H, and L.
  S = E + H + L  --- equation 3
  We can use equation 1 to express H + L in terms of x.
  H + L = 2x  --- equation 4
  Substituting equation 4 in equation 3, we get S = E + 2x
  Substituting equation 2 in the above equation, we get yz = E + 2x
  Therefore, E = yz - 2x
  Hence, the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is E/(z-2) = (yz - 2x)/(z-2)
  The answer is D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2)
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let the lowest score be L and the highest score be H.
  The average of the highest score and the lowest score is (H + L) / 2 = x.
  Therefore, H + L = 2x.
  Let S be the sum of all the scores in the class.
  Then, S = H + L + sum of all other scores.
  The average score for the entire class is y = S / z.
  We want to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers.
  Let the sum of all other scores be A.
  Then, the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is A / (z - 2).
  We need to find A.
  A = S - H - L = S - 2x (since H + L = 2x).
  y = S / z => S = yz.
  Therefore, A = yz - 2x.
  The average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is A / (z - 2) = (yz - 2x)/(z - 2).
  The answer is D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2).

  We need to find the sum of all the scores except the highest and lowest which is equal to the total sum minus the sum of the highest and lowest scores. Let's call the sum of all the scores as S.
  We know that the average score for the entire class is y. Therefore, S/z = y.
  We need to find the average of the scores excluding the highest and lowest scorers. Therefore, we divide the sum of all the scores except the highest and lowest by the number of students excluding the highest and lowest which is (z-2).
  Therefore, the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is (S-H-L)/(z-2).
  Since H+L = 2x, we can substitute it into the above equation to get (S-2x)/(z-2).
  We also know that S/z = y. Therefore, S = yz.
  Substituting S = yz into the above equation, we get (yz-2x)/(z-2).
  Therefore, the answer is D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2).
Action: Answer("D")

  B: 75 m
  C: 100 m
  D: 125 m
  E: 150 m

  Therefore, the speed of the space shuttle is 700/40 = 17.5 m/s
  The space shuttle will also travel a distance of 17.5 x 5 = 87.5 m in the 5 seconds it takes to pass a point.
  The length of the space shuttle is the sum of the distances it traveled in the 40 seconds it took to reach 700m and the 5 seconds it took to pass a point: 700m + 87.5m = 787.5m.
  Therefore, the length of the space shuttle is 787.5m which is equivalent to 787.5/6 = 131.25 meters (since 1 meter = 6 feet).

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 24 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, how many meters of fencing does she need?
Choices:
  A: 58
  B: 62
  C: 66
  D: 70
  E: 74
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let x be the width of the yard and y be the length of the yard.
  The area of the yard is xy = 240
  One side of the yard is not fenced, so the total length of fencing needed is the perimeter of the fenced area, which is 2x + y.
  We can solve for y in terms of x using xy = 240, so y = 240/x.
  Substituting y = 240/x in 2x + y, we get 2x + 240/x.
  To find the value of x that minimizes 2x + 240/x (and hence minimizes the length of fencing needed), we can take the derivative and set it to zero.
  The derivative of 2x + 240/x is 2 - 240/x^2.
  Setting 2 - 240/x^2 to zero and solving for x, we get x = 10.
  Therefore, the dimensions of the yard are 10 meters by 24 meters, and the length of fencing needed is 2(10) + 24 - 10 = 44 meters.
  The answer is C: 66.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume the length of the rectangular yard is L and the width is W.
  The area of the rectangular yard is given as LxW=240 sq.m.
  Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. This means that the perimeter of the fence is 2L + W - 10.
  We need to find the perimeter of the fence, which is 2L + W - 10.
  We can use the area formula to find one variable in terms of the other. 
  W = 240/L
  Substituting this in the fence perimeter equation, we get perimeter = 2L + 240/L - 10.
  To minimize the fence perimeter, we need to find the derivative of the perimeter equation and equate it to zero.
  dP/dL = 2 - 240/L^2 = 0
  Solving for L, we get L = sqrt(120).
  Substituting L in the perimeter equation, we get perimeter = 2*sqrt(120) + 10 = 2*2*sqrt(30) + 10 = 4sqrt(30) + 10.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 70.
Action: Answer("D") 
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Let's assume that the length of the yard is x meters.
  The area of a rectangle is the product of its length and width, so we have:
      x * y = 240, where y is the width of the yard.
  We also know that Alice is putting up fencing around three sides of the yard, which means she needs to fence:
      2 * x + y - 10 meters.
  We can now solve for y in the first equation:
      y = 240 / x
  We can substitute this expression for y into the second equation:
      2 * x + 240 / x - 10 = total fencing needed
  We can simplify this equation by multiplying everything by x:
      2x^2 + 240 - 10x = total fencing needed * x
  Rearranging the terms:
      2x^2 - 10x + 240 - total fencing needed * x = 0
  We can solve for x using the quadratic formula:
      x = [10 ± sqrt(10^2 - 4 * 2 * (240 - total fencing needed))]/(2 * 2)
      x = [5 ± sqrt(25 - 2 * (240 - total fencing needed))]/2
  We know that x must be greater than 10, since one side of the yard is already 10 meters. Therefore, we can discard the negative root:
      x = [5 + sqrt(25 - 2 * (240 - total fencing needed))]/2
  We can simplify this expression by combining like terms:
      x = [5 + sqrt(2 * total fencing needed - 175)]/2
  We can substitute this expression for x into the equation we derived earlier for the total fencing needed:
      2 * x + 240 / x - 10 = total fencing needed
  We can simplify this equation by substituting in our expression for x:
      5 + sqrt(2 * total fencing needed - 175) + 240 / [5 + sqrt(2 * total fencing needed - 175)] - 10 = total fencing needed
  We can now solve for total fencing needed by simplifying and isolating the square root term:
      sqrt(2 * total fencing needed - 175) = 15 - total fencing needed / 24
      2 * total fencing needed - 175 = (15 - total fencing needed / 24)^2
      2 * total fencing needed - 175 = 15^2 - 15 * total fencing needed / 12 + total fencing needed^2 / 576
      Multiplying everything by 576 to eliminate the fraction:
      1152 * total fencing needed - 92160 = 15^2 * 576 - 15 * 576 * total fencing needed + total fencing needed^2
      Simplifying:
      total fencing needed^2 - 15 * 576 * total fencing needed + 15^2 * 576 - 92160 + 2 * 5760 = 0
      total fencing needed^2 - 8640 * total fencing needed + 16560 = 0
  We can now solve for total fencing needed using the quadratic formula:
      total fencing needed = [8640 ± sqrt(8640^2 - 4 * 16560)]/2
      total fencing needed = [8640 ± 1960]/2
  We can discard the negative root, since the fencing needed must be a positive number:
      total fencing needed = [8640 + 1960]/2 = 5300/2 = 2650
  Therefore, Alice needs 2650 meters of fencing.

  Fencing length = 2x + y - 10 = 2(8) + 30 - 10 = 36.

  Let's assume the length of the rectangular yard is L and the width is W.
  The area of the rectangular yard is L * W = 240.
  We know that one side of the yard is 10 meters unfenced, so the length of the fence required will be L + W + L = 2L + W.
  We can rearrange the area formula to express the width in terms of length: W = 240 / L.
  Substituting W in the expression for the fence length, we have: 2L + W = 2L + 240 / L.
  To find the value of L that minimizes the fence length, we can take the derivative of the fence length expression, set it equal to zero, and solve for L.
  The derivative of 2L + 240 / L with respect to L is 2 - 240 / L^2.
  Setting this equal to zero, we get L = sqrt(120) = 10.95 (rounded to two decimal places).
  Therefore, the fence length required is 2L + W = 2(10.95) + 240 / 10.95 = 62.03 (rounded to two decimal places).
  The answer is B: 62.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 9:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the unfenced side of the rectangular yard is the length of the rectangle.
  Let the width of the rectangle be 'w'.
  Then, the area of the rectangular yard is length x width = 10w x w = 10w^2.
  The total area of the yard is given as 240 square meters.
  Therefore, 10w^2 = 240.
  Solving for w, we get w = 4*sqrt(15).
  The length of the other two sides of the rectangular yard is equal to 2w+10.
  Therefore, the total fencing required will be 2w+10+2w+10+w = 5w + 20.
  Substituting the value of w, we get the total fencing required as 5(4*sqrt(15)) + 20 = 70.89 (approx).
  The answer is closest to D: 70.

Topic: Math
Question: A sporting goods store carries only yellow and white golf balls. At the beginning of the day it had 600 golf balls in stock, and by the end of the day it had sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls. If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so sold all of its white golf balls, how many yellow golf balls did the store have to begin the day?
Choices:
  A: 80
  B: 120
  C: 240
  D: 320
  E: 360
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's assume that the store had "x" yellow golf balls and "y" white golf balls.
  We know that the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls.
  We also know that the store sold all of its white golf balls.
  So, the store had only yellow golf balls left at the end of the day.
  Therefore, 80% of the inventory of golf balls at the beginning of the day was equal to "x" + "y" - "y" = "x".
  80% of 600 = 480.
  So, x = 480.
  Therefore, the store had 480 yellow golf balls to begin the day.
  The answer is E: 360.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, then the remaining 20% of the inventory that was not sold must also be an equal number of yellow and white golf balls.
  If all of the white golf balls were sold, then the number of yellow golf balls remaining at the end of the day must be equal to 20% of the initial number of yellow golf balls.
  Therefore, the number of yellow golf balls remaining at the end of the day is equal to the number of white golf balls sold, which is equal to 0.5 * 600 * 0.8 = 240.
  This means that the initial number of yellow golf balls must have been 240 / 0.2 = 1200.
  Therefore, the initial number of yellow golf balls was 1200 - 600 = 600.
  The answer is 600, which corresponds to choice A.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 26 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The bus fare for two persons for travelling between Agra and Aligarh id four-thirds the train fare between the same places for one person. The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512. Find the train fare between the two places for one person?
Choices:
  A: 126
  B: 77
  C: 88
  D: 66
  E: 54
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person is X.
  The bus fare for two persons for travelling between Agra and Aligarh is (4/3)X.
  The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus is 6*(4/3)X = 8X.
  The total fare paid by 8 persons travelling by train is 8X.
  The sum of the total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train is given as Rs. 1512. Therefore, we can write the equation:
  
  8X + 6*(4/3)X = 1512
  
  Solving the above equation, we get:
  
  X = 126
  
  Therefore, the train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person is Rs. 126.
  The answer is A: 126.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's assume that the train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person is "x".
Then, the bus fare for two persons will be (4/3)*x.
The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs. 1512.
Let's find the total fare for the bus ride first.
For 6 persons, the number of bus tickets required will be (6/2)=3.
Therefore, the total fare for bus travel will be 3*(4/3)*x = 4x.
Similarly, for 8 persons travelling by train, the total fare will be 8*x = 8x.
The sum of the fares for bus and train travel is given as Rs. 1512.
Therefore, the equation will be 4x + 8x = 1512
Simplifying the above equation, we get 12x = 1512
Solving this equation, we get x = 126
Therefore, the train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person is Rs. 126.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 27 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Jim filled his dog's bowl with dog food. Starting at 8:00 am, Jim's dog ate exactly once an hour, consuming exactly 1/3 of the dog food remaining in the bowl at each feeding session. Approximately, what percent of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon of the same day?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 25%
  C: 30%
  D: 35%
  E: 40%
Response 0:
Thought:
  The dog eats once an hour for 4 hours which means the dog ate 4 times.
  At each feeding, the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining food.
  Therefore, the dog consumed (1/3)^4 of the original food by noon.
  We can calculate this as (1/3)^4 = 1/81.
  So, the amount of food remaining in the bowl is 80/81 of the original amount.
  To find the percentage, we can take 80/81 and multiply it by 100.
  This gives us 98.77, which is approximately 100.
  Therefore, approximately 100% - 25% (1/4) = 75% of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") - None of the answer choices are close enough to 75%, which is the correct answer.
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Jim's dog ate once every hour, and consumed 1/3 of the remaining dog food in the bowl.
  This means that after the first hour, 2/3 of the original food was left.
  After the second hour, (2/3) * (2/3) = 4/9 of the original food was left.
  After the third hour, (4/9) * (2/3) = 8/27 of the original food was left.
  After the fourth hour (which was at noon), (8/27) * (2/3) = 16/81 of the original food was left.
  This means that right before the dog began to eat at noon, 16/81 of the original food was still in the bowl.
  To convert this fraction to a percentage, we can multiply by 100: (16/81) * 100 = 19.75, which rounds to approximately 20.
  Therefore, the answer is approximately 20%.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 28 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300 after the price of each article decreased by 15%. What is the new selling price of each article?
Choices:
  A: $8
  B: $10
  C: $13.6
  D: $22.9
  E: $40
Response 0:
Thought:
- If Anna can buy 5 more articles for $300, that means each article costs $60 ($300/5).
- If the price of each article decreased by 15%, that means Anna is paying only 85% of the original price for each article.
- Let's assume the original price of each article was x. Then, 85% of x would be (85/100)x = 0.85x.
- We know that 0.85x = 60 (the new price of each article after the discount).
- Solving for x, we get x = 70.59.
- Therefore, the original price of each article was $70.59, and the new selling price of each article after the 15% discount is $60.
- The answer is not one of the available choices. Therefore, the most likely answer is C: $13.6. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300, which means the price of each article decreased by 15%.
  Let the original selling price of each article be x. Then, the new selling price after the 15% discount is (x - 0.15x) = 0.85x.
  If Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300 at the new selling price, then the total cost of 5 articles is 5 * 0.85x = 4.25x.
  Therefore, 4.25x = 300, and solving for x gives x = 70.59.
  So, the new selling price of each article is 0.85x = 0.85 * 70.59 = $60.
  The answer is not one of the choices.

Question: A rope 20 meters long is cut into two pieces. If the length of one piece of rope is 3 meters shorter than the length of the other, what is the length, in meters, of the longer piece of rope?

  A: 7.5
  B: 8.9
  C: 9.9
  D: 11.5
  E: 11.7

  So, x + (x - 3) = 20.
  Solving for x gives x = 11.5.
  Therefore, the length of the longer piece of rope is 11.5 meters.
  The answer is D: 11.5.

  C: 32
  D: 25
  E: 18

  If each song was selected 5 times, then there were a total of 10 x 5 = 50 votes cast.
  Each student selected 2 songs, so the number of students surveyed is 50 / 2 = 25.
  The answer is D: 25.
Action: Answer("D")

  Since each student made 20 song selections, the total number of students surveyed can be found by dividing the total number of song selections by the number of song selections made by each student: 50/20 = 2.5.
  Since the number of students must be a whole number, the answer is either 2 or 3.

  Therefore, the answer is C: 32.

Question: The original retail price of an appliance was 60 percent more than its wholesale cost. If the appliance was actually sold for 20 percent less than the original retail price, then it was sold for what percent more than its wholesale cost?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 28%
  C: 36%
  D: 40%
  E: 42%
Response 0:
Thought:
Assume that the Wholesale cost of the appliance is $100, then
Original retail price = 60% of $100 +$100 = $160.
20% less than the original retail price = 80% of $160 = $128.
The difference between the selling price and wholesale cost = $128 - $100 = $28.
The percentage more than the wholesale cost = (28/100) x 100 = 28%
Therefore, the answer is B: 28%.
Action: Answer("B")

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 32 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: When folded into two equal halves a rectangular sheet had a perimeter of 48cm for each part folded along one set of sides and the same is 66cm when folded along the other set of sides. Find the area of the sheet.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 1120
  C: 792
  D: 1320
  E: 1200
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the length of the sheet is 'l' and the breadth of the sheet is 'b'.
  When folded along one set of sides, each part will have a perimeter of 48cm. So, the length of each part will be l/2 and the breadth of each part will be b. Therefore, 2(l/2 + b) = 48.
  When folded along the other set of sides, each part will have a perimeter of 66cm. So, the length of each part will be l and the breadth of each part will be b/2. Therefore, 2(l + b/2) = 66.
  We can solve these two equations to get the values of 'l' and 'b'.
  Once we have 'l' and 'b', we can find the area of the sheet by multiplying 'l' and 'b'.
Action: Answer("D") 1320
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the length and breadth of the rectangular sheet be L and B, respectively.
  When folded along one set of sides, the perimeter of each part is 48cm. So, the length of each part is L/2 and the perimeter of each part = 2L/2 + B = L + B = 48.
  When folded along the other set of sides, the perimeter of each part is 66cm. So, the length of each part is B/2 and the perimeter of each part = 2B/2 + L = B + L = 66.
  We can solve these two equations simultaneously to get L = 18 and B = 30.
  Therefore, the area of the sheet = L * B = 18 * 30 = 540 sq.cm.
  The answer is not one of the choices given, but the correct answer is E: None of the above.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let the length and breadth of the rectangular sheet be l and b respectively.
  The perimeter of the rectangle is 2(l+b).
  When folded along length, the perimeter becomes 48cm for each part folded, so the length of the paper is divided into two equal parts i.e. l/2 = 24cm
  Therefore, 2(l+b) = 2(24+2b).
  By simplifying the above equation we get, l = 48-2b.
  Similarly, when folded along breadth, the breadth of the paper is divided into two equal parts i.e. b/2 = 33cm.
  Therefore, 2(l+b) = 2(33+2l).
  By simplifying the above equation we get, b = 66-2l.
  We can substitute the value of l and find the value of b, and then we can calculate the area using the formula, Area = Length x Breadth.
  The answer is A: 1584.

So, after folding, the length of each part is (66/2) - l = 33 - l.
Similarly, the breadth of each part is (66/2) - b = 33 - b.
The total area of the sheet is l * b.
We can get two equations from the above information and solve for l and b to get the area of the sheet.

Equation 1: 2(24 - b) + 2l = 48
Simplifying Equation 1: l + 24 - b = 24
                      l = b

Equation 2: 2(33 - l) + 2b = 66
Simplifying Equation 2: b + 33 - l = 33
                      b = l

2(24 - l) + 2l = 48
Simplifying this equation, we get:
l = 12

2(33 - l) + 2l = 66
Simplifying this equation, we get:
l = 11

  The perimeter of the rectangular sheet, P = 2(L+W).
  When folded along the length, each part of the sheet has a perimeter of 48cm. Therefore, the length of each part is 24cm.
  When folded along the width, each part of the sheet has a perimeter of 66cm. Therefore, the width of each part is 33cm.

  2(L + W) = 48
  2(L + W) = 66
  By solving these equations, we can find the value of L and W.
  Then, the area of the rectangular sheet, A = L x W.

  From 2(L + W) = 48, we get L + W = 24.
  From 2(L + W) = 66, we get L + W = 33.
  Subtracting the first equation from the second equation, we get W = 9.
  Substituting W = 9 in L + W = 24, we get L = 15.
  Therefore, the area of the rectangular sheet, A = L x W = 15 x 9 = 135 sq.cm.

  Then, the perimeter of the sheet is given by: 2(l+w).
  When folded along one set of sides, each part has a perimeter of 48cm.
  So, the length of each part is (48/2) - w = 24 - w.
  Also, the width of each part is w.
  Therefore, the area of each part is (24-w) * w = 24w - w^2.
  Similarly, when folded along the other set of sides, each part has a perimeter of 66cm.
  So, the length of each part is (66/2) - w = 33 - w.
  Also, the width of each part is w.
  Therefore, the area of each part is (33-w) * w = 33w - w^2.
  We know that the two parts are equal in area.
  Therefore, 24w - w^2 = 33w - w^2.
  Solving for w, we get w = 11.
  Substituting w=11 in 24w - w^2, we get the area of each part = 264 sq.cm.
  Therefore, the area of the sheet is (2 * 264) = 528 sq.cm.
  The answer is D: 1320.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 9:
Thought:
  Let L and B be the length and breadth of the rectangular sheet respectively.
  When folded along the length L/2 + B = 48.
  When folded along the breadth B/2 + L = 66.
  Solving these equations simultaneously, we get L = 24cm and B = 18cm.
  Therefore, the area of the sheet = L * B = 24 * 18 = 432 sq cm.

Question: On a normal day Bill usually averages about 15 mph when riding his bicycle. On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph. How far can Bill travel on a windy day in 21 minutes? Round to the nearest hundredth.
Choices:
  A: 2 miles
  B: 2.25 miles
  C: 3.25 miles
  D: 3.85 miles
  E: 2.85 miles
Response 0:
Thought:
  On a normal day, Bill's speed is 15 mph.
  On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph, so his speed is 15 - 4 = 11 mph.
  We need to find how far Bill can travel in 21 minutes.
  There are 60 minutes in an hour, so 21 minutes is 21/60 = 0.35 hours.
  To find the distance, we can use the formula distance = speed x time.
  The speed is 11 mph and the time is 0.35 hours.
  So the distance is 11 x 0.35 = 3.85 miles.
  Rounded to the nearest hundredth, the answer is D: 3.85 miles.
Action: Answer("D")

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 34 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In a bag of red and green sweets, the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4. If the bag contains 120 green sweets, how many red sweets are there?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 80
  C: 95
  D: 100
  E: 85
Response 0:
Thought:
  Given the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  Let's assume the common ratio between red and green sweets as x.
  Therefore, the number of red sweets would be 3x and the number of green sweets would be 4x.
  As per the question, the bag contains 120 green sweets.
  Equating 4x = 120, we get the value of x as 30.
  Therefore, the number of red sweets would be 3x = 3*30 = 90.
  The answer is A: 90.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  This means that for every 3 red sweets, there are 4 green sweets.
  We know that there are 120 green sweets.
  To find the number of red sweets, we need to use the ratio.
  If there are 4 green sweets for every 3 red sweets, then we can write this as 4/3.
  We can use this ratio to find the number of red sweets:
  4/3 = 120/x (where x is the number of red sweets)
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = (3/4) * 120
  x = 90
  Therefore, there are 90 red sweets.
  The answer is A: 90.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  This means that for every 3 red sweets, there are 4 green sweets in the bag.
  We are given that there are 120 green sweets in the bag.
  We can find the number of red sweets by setting up a proportion:
  3/4 = x/120, where x is the number of red sweets.
  To solve for x, we can cross-multiply:
  4x = 3 * 120
  4x = 360
  x = 90
  Therefore, there are 90 red sweets in the bag.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 35 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A number of friends decided to go on a picnic and planned to spend Rs. 96 on eatables. Four of them, however, did not turn up. As a consequence, the remaining ones had to contribute Rs. 4 extra, each. The number of those who attended the picnic was
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 12
  C: 16
  D: 24
  E: 25
Response 0:
Thought:
Let "x" be the number of friends that actually attended the picnic.
If all friends were present, the cost per person would be Rs. 96/x.
Since the four friends did not turn up, the cost per person increased to Rs. 96/(x-4).
We can create an equation based on the given information: Rs. 96/x + Rs. 4 = Rs. 96/(x-4).
We can solve for "x" to find the number of friends that attended the picnic.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's assume the number of friends who decided to go on the picnic is "x".
The amount they planned to spend is Rs. 96.
4 of them did not turn up, so the remaining people attended the picnic.
Each of the remaining people had to contribute Rs. 4 extra, so the total extra amount collected = (4 * (x-4)) = (4x - 16).
The total amount collected after the 4 people did not turn up = Rs. 96 + (4x - 16).
The total amount collected by each of the remaining attendees = (96 + (4x - 16)) / (x - 4).
According to the problem, each attendee had to contribute Rs. 4 extra. So, we can set up the following equation: (96 + (4x - 16)) / (x - 4) = 4.
Solving this equation, we get x = 12.
Therefore, the number of those who attended the picnic was 12.
The answer is B: 12.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 37 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: there are more than 501 students in a school such that 20% of them exactly took physics and 28% of them exactly took math. What could be the least possible no of students in the school?
Choices:
  A: 550
  B: 570
  C: 600
  D: 700
  E: none of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are n students in the school.
  According to the problem, 20% of n took physics, and 28% of n took math.
  We don't know what percentage of students took both physics and math.
  We can use the fact that the sum of the percentages of students who took physics and math is greater than 50%.
  Using this information, we can create an inequality and solve for n to find the least possible number of students.

Calculation:
  Let P be the percentage of students who took physics and math.
  Therefore, we have: 20% + 28% - P% > 50%
  Simplifying: 48% - P% > 50%
  Subtracting 48% from both sides: -P% > 2%
  Multiplying both sides by -1: P% < -2%
  Since P% is a percentage, it must be between 0% and 100%.
  Therefore, there is no solution to the inequality, and none of the choices is correct.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let's assume that there are n students in the school.
  According to the question, 20% of n students took physics. Which means that 0.2n students took physics.
  Also, 28% of n students took Math. Which means that 0.28n students took Math.
  We know that the total number of students who took physics and math is more than 501. Therefore:
  0.2n + 0.28n > 501
  0.48n > 501
  n > 1043.75
  Since the number of students must be a whole number, the least possible number of students is 1044.
  The answer is E: none of these.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought:
Let's assume 'x' is the total number of students in the school.
20% of the students took physics, which means 0.2x students took physics.
28% of the students took math, which means 0.28x students took math.
The minimum number of total students will occur when all physics students are different than math students. This means that the number of physics students and math students does not overlap.
The minimum total number of students can be found by adding the minimum number of students who took physics and the minimum number of students who took math.
The minimum number of physics students is 20% of the total number of students because all physics students are different from math students.
The minimum number of math students is 28% of the total number of students because all math students are different from physics students.
Therefore, the minimum number of students is 20% of x plus 28% of x, which equals 48% of x.
0.48x > 501 (because the total number of students is more than 501)
x > 1043.75

Question: Two cars are travelling from the same starting point in the same direction, having started their commute at the same time. The first car travels at a steady rate of 55 mph, while the second travels at a steady rate of 52 mph. How much time will pass before the cars are 15 miles away from each other?
Choices:
  A: 3 hours
  B: 5 hours
  C: 6 hours
  D: 4 hours
  E: 7 hours
Response 0:
Thought:
  The first car is travelling faster than the second car.
  The distance between them will increase at a rate of 55 mph - 52 mph = 3 mph.
  We want to find out how long it takes for the distance between them to be 15 miles.
  We can use the formula: time = distance / rate.
  Time = 15 miles / 3 mph = 5 hours.
  Therefore, it takes 5 hours for the cars to be 15 miles away from each other.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The second car is travelling slower than the first car.
  The distance between the two cars will increase at a rate of 3 mph (55 mph - 52 mph).
  To find how much time it will take for the two cars to be 15 miles apart, we can set up an equation using distance, rate, and time formula, which is: distance = rate x time.
  Let d be the distance the second car has travelled when the two cars are 15 miles apart.
  Then, the distance the first car has travelled is d + 15 miles.

    d + 15 = 3t

    d = 52t
    52t + 15 = 3t
    49t = 15
    t = 15/49 hours

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 40 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Suppose for any real number x, [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x. Let L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] and R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]. Then it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which
Choices:
  A: L(x,y) = R(x,y)
  B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y)
  C: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  D: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's consider option A first. If L(x,y) = R(x,y), then we have:
  [x] + [y] + [x + y] = [2x] + [2y]
  We know that [x + y] ≤ [2x + 2y]. Therefore, [x] + [y] + [x + y] ≤ [2x] + [2y] + [x + y] ≤ [2x] + [2y] + [2x + 2y]. 
  Since [a + b] ≤ [a] + [b], we have [x] + [y] + [x + y] ≤ [2x] + [2y] + [2x] + [2y] = 2([2x] + [2y]). 
  Hence,  [x] + [y] + [x + y] is even. Since [x], [y], and [x + y] are all integers, either all of them are even or all of them are odd. 
  If all of them are even, then we can write x = a + p, y = b + q, and x + y = c + r for some integers a, b, c, p, q, and r such that 0 ≤ p, q, r < 1. 
  Then L(x,y) = a + b + c and R(x,y) = 2a + 2b. But a + b + c is odd and 2a + 2b is even, so they cannot be equal. 
  If all of them are odd, then we can write x = a + p + 0.5, y = b + q + 0.5, and x + y = c + r + 0.5 for some integers a, b, c, p, q, and r such that 0 ≤ p, q, r < 1. 
  Then L(x,y) = a + b + c + 1 and R(x,y) = 2a + 2b. But a + b + c + 1 is even and 2a + 2b is even, so they cannot be equal. 
  Therefore, it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which L(x,y) = R(x,y). 
  The answer is A: L(x,y) = R(x,y).
Action: Answer("A")

  Since we are rounding down, R(x,y) will always be greater than or equal to L(x,y).

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 41 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: While selling a watch, a shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%. If he gives a discount of 7%, he earns Rs. 15 less as profit. The marked price of the watch is:
Choices:
  A: Rs. 697.50
  B: Rs. 712.50
  C: Rs. 787.50
  D: Rs. 750
  E: Rs. 780
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let’s assume the marked price of the watch is M.
  If he gives a discount of 5%, then the selling price will be 0.95M and he will make a profit of P.
  If he gives a discount of 7%, then the selling price will be 0.93M and he will make a profit of P - 15.
  We know that the profit percentage is calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) * 100.
  The cost price of the watch is the same in both cases, so we can set up an equation:
  (P/M) * 100 = [(P - 15)/M] * 100 * 93/95
  Solving this equation gives us P = M/20.
  Now we can use this value to solve for the marked price:
  0.95M = M - (M/20)
  M = Rs. 712.50
  Therefore, the marked price of the watch is Rs. 712.50.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let the marked price of the watch be M.
  The shopkeeper gave a discount of 5%, so he sold the watch for 0.95M.
  The shopkeeper gave a discount of 7%, so he sold the watch for 0.93M.
  The difference in profit is Rs. 15.
  Therefore, 0.02M = 15 or M = 750.
  The marked price of the watch is Rs. 750.

  B: 651
  C: 400

  Value of x number of 1 rupee coins = 1x.

  Therefore, there are 400 of each type of coin.

Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is:
Choices:
  A: 2.6m
  B: 3.9m
  C: 4m
  D: 4.2m
  E: 4.4m

  The cost of papering the walls is (perimeter x height) x cost per meter of paper.
  The area of the doors and windows is subtracted from the area of the walls.
  We can write two equations based on the given information and solve for x.
  Once we find x, we can calculate the height of the room.

Response 1:
Thought:
  Let the height of the room be '2x'. Then, its semi-perimeter is (5x/2) * 2 = 5x.
  Let the length and breadth of the room be 'l' and 'b' respectively.
  We know that the cost of papering the walls is Rs.260. The area of the walls is (2x + l + b) * l = (2x + l + b) * b.
  The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m. Therefore, the area of the walls excluding the doors and windows is (2x + l + b) * b - 15.
  The area of the walls is equal to the cost of papering them. Thus, (2x + l + b) * b * 2 * (1/100) = 260.
  Simplifying, we get b^2 + (2x + l)b - 6500 = 0.
  Using the quadratic formula, we get b = (-2x - l + 130sqrt(2x + l + 169))/2 and b = (-2x - l - 130sqrt(2x + l + 169))/2.
  Since the length and breadth of the room cannot be negative, we need to choose the positive value of 'b'.
  We know that the ratio of the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. Thus, 2x/5x = 2/5. Solving for 'x', we get x = 5.
  Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 2 * 5 = 10 meters.
  The answer is not given in meters, but in this case, it is helpful to solve in meters to eliminate any unit conversion errors.

  Using the above information, we can form equations and solve for x.

Solution:
  Let's start by finding the length and breadth of the room.
  semi-perimeter = length + breadth
  5y = length + breadth
  Now, let's find the area of the room.
  area = length * breadth
  area = (5y/2 - x) * (5y/2)
  area = (5y^2/4 - xy)
  We know that the cost of papering the walls is Rs. 260 with width 50cm and Rs. 2 per meter.
  So, the total length of paper required = (length + breadth) * height * 2
  total length of paper required = (5y/2 + x) * 2x * 2
  total length of paper required = 4x(5y/2 + x)
  total length of paper required = 10xy + 8x^2
  Total cost of papering walls = Length of paper required * Cost per meter
  260 = (10xy + 8x^2) * 2
  130 = 5xy + 4x^2
  We also know that area of doors and windows is 15 sq.m.
  area of doors and windows = length * breadth - area of doors and windows
  15 = (5y/2 - x) * x - 15
  30 = 5x^2 - 5xy
  Now, we have two equations,
  130 = 5xy + 4x^2
  30 = 5x^2 - 5xy
  Let's solve them simultaneously.
  Adding both equations, we get
  160 = 9x^2
  x^2 = 160/9
  x = sqrt(160)/3
  x = (4 * sqrt(10))/3
  Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = (8 * sqrt(10))/3 = 2.6m (approx).

Thought:
  Let h be the height of the room.
  Let p be the semi-perimeter of the room.
  We know that h/p = 2/5.
  We need to find the height of the room, so we need to find h.
  We can find the area of the walls by subtracting the area of the doors and windows from the total area.
  We can then find the length of the walls using the area and the width of the paper.
  We can find the cost of the paper by multiplying the length of the walls by the cost per meter.
  We can then solve for h using the equation h/p = 2/5.
  
  Let's start solving the problem.

Action: 
The area of the room is (2p * h) sq.m.
The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m.
So, the area of the walls is (2p * h) - 15 sq.m.

The width of the paper is 50 cm = 0.5 m.
So, the length of the walls is [(2p * h) - 15]/0.5 m = 4p * h - 30 m.

The cost of the paper is (4p * h - 30) * 2 Rs = (8p * h - 60) Rs.

We know that h/p = 2/5, so h = (2/5) * p.
Substituting this into the equation for the cost of the paper, we get:
(8p * (2/5)p - 60) = 16p^2/5 - 60.

We are given that the cost of the paper is Rs.260, so:
16p^2/5 - 60 = 260.

Solving for p, we get:
p^2 = 400/4 = 100.
p = 10.

Substituting this value of p into the equation for h, we get:
h = (2/5) * 10 = 4.

Therefore, the height of the room is 4m.

Response 9:
Thought:
  Let's use h to represent the height of the room.
  Let's use s to represent the semi-perimeter of the room.
  Then, according to the problem, we have h:s/2 = 2:5.
  Rearranging this equation, we get s = 2h(5/2) = 5h.
  Let's use l to represent the length of the room.
  Then, the cost of papering the walls is the cost of the wallpaper multiplied by the total length of the walls.
  The total length of the walls is the perimeter of the room minus the area of the doors and windows.
  The perimeter of the room is s + 2h = 5h + 2h = 7h.
  The area of the doors and windows is given as 15 sq.m.
  Therefore, the total length of the walls is 7h - 15/0.5 = 7h - 30.
  Putting it all together, we get:
  260 = 2(7h - 30)(l/100)
  130 = (7h - 30)(l/100)
  13000 = (7h - 30)l
  13000 = (7h - 30)(2h/5)
  13000 = 14h^2/5 - 6h
  Rearranging this equation, we get:
  14h^2/5 - 6h - 13000 = 0
  Multiplying both sides by 5, we get:
  14h^2 - 30h - 65000 = 0
  Factoring out 2 from the coefficients, we get:
  2(7h^2 - 15h - 32500) = 0
  We can then use the quadratic formula to solve for h:
  h = (-b ± sqrt(b^2 - 4ac)) / 2a
  where a = 7, b = -15, and c = -32500.
  Plugging in these values, we get:
  h = (15 ± sqrt(15^2 - 4(7)(-32500))) / 2(7)
  h = (15 ± sqrt(422965)) / 14
  h ≈ 4.2 or h ≈ -16.4
  Since h represents the height of the room, which cannot be negative, we choose h ≈ 4.2.
  Therefore, the height of the room is approximately 4.2m.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 44 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hrs and at 4 kmph for 12 hrs. His average speed is
Choices:
  A: 4 1/3 km/h
  B: 7 2/3 km/h
  C: 9 ½ km/h
  D: 8 km/h
  E: 81 km/h
Response 0:
Thought:
  To find average speed, we use the formula: 
  Average speed = Total distance covered / Total time taken.
  Let's find the total distance covered.
  Distance covered at 5 kmph for 6 hrs = 5 kmph x 6 hrs = 30 km
  Distance covered at 4 kmph for 12 hrs = 4 kmph x 12 hrs = 48 km
  Total distance covered = 30 km + 48 km = 78 km
  Total time taken = 6 hrs + 12 hrs = 18 hrs
  Average speed = 78 km / 18 hrs = 13/3 km/h ≈ 4 1/3 km/h
  Therefore, the answer is A: 4 1/3 km/h.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  To find the average speed, we need to know the total distance traveled and the total time taken.
  The distance traveled at 5 km/h for 6 hours is 5 km/h x 6 h = 30 km.
  The distance traveled at 4 km/h for 12 hours is 4 km/h x 12 h = 48 km.
  The total distance traveled is 30 km + 48 km = 78 km.
  The total time taken is 6 hours + 12 hours = 18 hours.
  Therefore, the average speed is 78 km / 18 h = 4 1/3 km/h.
  The answer is A: 4 1/3 km/h.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 46 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The difference between the squares of two numbers is 256000 and the sum of the numbers is 1000. The numbers are
Choices:
  A: 600, 400
  B: 628, 372
  C: 640, 360
  D: None of these
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the numbers be x and y.
  The difference between the squares of two numbers is (x^2 - y^2) = 256000.
  The sum of the numbers is x + y = 1000.
  We can use the following formula to factorize the difference of squares: x^2 - y^2 = (x + y)(x - y).
  We can substitute these values into the equation and solve for x and y.
  (x + y)(x - y) = 256000
  x + y = 1000
  We can use elimination method to solve for x and y.
  Adding the two equations we get:
  2x = 1256
  x = 628
  Substituting x in the equation x + y = 1000, we get:
  y = 372
  Therefore, the numbers are 628 and 372.
  The answer is B: 628, 372.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the two numbers are x and y.
  According to the problem, x^2 - y^2 = 256000 and x + y = 1000.
  We can factor x^2 - y^2 as (x - y) * (x + y).
  Substituting, we get (x - y) * 1000 = 256000.
  Simplifying further, we get x - y = 256.
  Adding (x + y) and (x - y), we get 2x = 1256.
  Solving for x, we get x = 628.
  Substituting x = 628 in x + y = 1000, we get y = 372.
  Therefore, the two numbers are 628 and 372.
  The answer is B: 628, 372.
Action: Answer("B")

  x^2 - y^2 = (x + y)(x - y) = 1000(x - y) = 256000
  Therefore, x - y = 256
  Now, we have two equations:
  x + y = 1000
  x - y = 256
  Solving these equations simultaneously gives x = 628 and y = 372.
  Therefore, the numbers are 628 and 372.
  The answer is B: 628, 372.

Response 8:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the two numbers are x and y.
  According to the problem statement, we can write two equations:
    x^2 - y^2 = 256000  (Equation 1)
    x + y = 1000        (Equation 2)
  We can use Equation 1 to express y in terms of x:
    y^2 = x^2 - 256000
    y = sqrt(x^2 - 256000)
  We can then substitute this expression for y into Equation 2:
    x + sqrt(x^2 - 256000) = 1000
  We can solve for x by squaring both sides of the equation:
    x^2 + (x^2 - 256000) + 2x*sqrt(x^2 - 256000) = 1000^2
    2x*sqrt(x^2 - 256000) = 744000
    x*sqrt(x^2 - 256000) = 372000
    x^2*(x^2 - 256000) = 372000^2
    x^4 - 256000*x^2 - 13838400000 = 0
  Now, we can solve for x using the quadratic formula:
    x^2 = (256000 +/- sqrt(256000^2 + 4*13838400000))/2
    x^2 = 128000 +/- 8000*sqrt(69)
    x ≈ 640 or x ≈ -640
  We can discard the negative value of x, and use x = 640 to find y:
    y = sqrt(x^2 - 256000) ≈ 360

  The answer is C: 640, 360.

Response 9:
Thought:
  Let x and y be the two numbers.
  We have two equations: x^2 - y^2 = 256000 and x + y = 1000.
  We can factor the first equation as (x+y)(x-y) = 256000.
  From the second equation, we can solve for x in terms of y as x = 1000 - y.
  Substituting into the factored form of the first equation, we get (1000-2y)(x-y) = 256000.
  We can simplify to get y^2 - 500y + 128000 = 0.
  This quadratic equation can be factored as (y-320)(y-180) = 0.
  Therefore, the possible values for y are 180 and 320.
  Substituting into x = 1000 - y, we get x = 820 and x = 680, respectively.
  Therefore, the numbers are 680 and 320 or 820 and 180.
  Checking, we find that (820)^2 - (180)^2 = 256000 and 820 + 180 = 1000.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 640, 360.

Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ?
Choices:
  A: 226
  B: 230
  C: 240
  D: 260
  E: 280
Response 0:
Thought:
  This is a problem involving profit and loss.
  Yearly profit should be greater than or equal to $626,400.
  The company produces 420 units every month.
  There are 12 months in a year, so the company produces 420 x 12 = 5,040 units in a year.
  The production cost per component is $110.
  Therefore, the total production cost in a year is 5,040 x 110 = $554,400.
  To make a profit of $626,400, the total revenue in a year should be 626,400 + 554,400 = $1,180,800.
  The selling price per component should be at least 1,180,800 / 5,040 = $234
  The minimum selling price per component should be $234 or more.
  The answer is not A, B, D, or E.
Action: Answer("C")

The yearly profit is equal to the revenue from selling minus the production costs. 
The revenue is the selling price per component multiplied by the number of components sold in a year (12 months x 420 units per month = 5040 units).
The profit function is given by Profit = (selling price per component x 5040) - (110 x 5040).

Profit = (selling price x 5040) - (110 x 5040)
Profit = 5040(selling price - 110)
To guarantee a profit of $626,400 or more, we need:
Profit >= 626400
5040(selling price - 110) >= 626400
selling price - 110 >= 124
selling price >= 234
Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee a yearly profit of $626,400 or more is $234.

Question: If m > 0, y > 0, and x is m percent of 4y, then, in terms of y, m is what percentage of x?

  B: 4y
  C: 50y
  D: 2500/y
  E: 5000/y

  From the given equation, m = (x / 4y) * 100
  To express m as a percentage of x, we divide m by x and multiply by 100.
  Therefore, m as a percentage of x is (m/x) * 100 = [(x / 4y) * 100 / x] * 100 = (25 / y) * 1%, or 25/y expressed as a percentage.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 2500/y.

Question: What should come in place of the question mark(?) in each of the following questions ?
a2 - b2/(a + b)2 (?)=(a - b)2
Choices:
  A: (a + b)(a - b)
  B: (a - b)2
  C: (a + b)2
  D: a3 + b3
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought: 
  We can solve the given equation by using the identity (a+b)^2 = a^2 + 2ab + b^2
  Therefore, (a+b)^2 = a^2 + 2ab + b^2, and (a-b)^2 = a^2 - 2ab + b^2
  Let's substitute these values in the given equation:
  a2 - b2/(a + b)2 = (a - b)2
  (a2 + b2 + 2ab - b2)/(a + b)2 = (a2 + b2 - 2ab)
  2ab/(a + b)2 = 2ab - 2ab
  2ab/(a + b)2 = 0
  2ab = 0
  ab = 0
  Therefore, either 'a' or 'b' is equal to zero.
  Let's substitute a=0 and b=1 in the given equation:
  a2 - b2/(a + b)2 = (a - b)2
  0 - 1/(0 + 1)2 = (0 - 1)2
  -1 = 1, which is not possible.
  Let's substitute a=1 and b=0 in the given equation:
  a2 - b2/(a + b)2 = (a - b)2
  1 - 0/(1 + 0)2 = (1 - 0)2
  1 = 1, which is true.
  Therefore, the correct answer is (a + b)2.
  The answer is C: (a + b)2.

### Temperature: 7.0 | Problem 54 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Everyone in the family earns money each month. If the total income of a family per month is $9000 and the median income is $3000, how many members are there in the family?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 3
  C: 4
  D: 5
  E: 6
Response 0:
Thought:
  The median income is the income of the middle person in the family when incomes are listed in order.
  If the median income is $3000, then there must be someone who earns $3000 in the family.
  Let's assume there are 'n' members in the family.
  If the median income is $3000, and there are 'n' members in the family, then the sum of all incomes must be 3 times the median income: 3 * 3000 = 9000.
  Therefore, there are 'n' members in the family, and the total income is $9000. We need to find the value of 'n'.
  Let's assume the family members earn the same amount of money. In this case, the total income of the family can be divided equally among all members: 9000/n.
  If we divide the total income by the number of members, we get the income per person: 9000/n.
  If the income per person is $3000, then we can write an equation: 9000/n = 3000.
  Solving for 'n', we can get the answer.
  n = 9000/3000
  n = 3
  Therefore, there are 3 members in the family.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Median income is the income that is exactly in the middle when all the incomes are arranged in order from lowest to highest.
  Let's assume there are 'n' members in the family.
  If we sort the incomes in ascending order, then the median income will be the (n+1)/2-th income if 'n' is odd. If 'n' is even, then the median income will be the average of the n/2-th income and the (n/2)+1-th income.
  From the given information, we know that median income is $3000. Therefore, the total income of the family earned by the members who earn less than $3000 must be equal to the total income earned by the members who earn more than $3000.
  Let's assume there are 'm' members who earn less than $3000. Then there are 'n-m' members who earn more than $3000.
  So, we have two equations:
  m x p + (n-m) x q = 9000  ... (1)
  p x m < 3000 <= q x (n-m)  ... (2)
  Here, p is the income earned by the members who earn less than $3000 and q is the income earned by the members who earn more than $3000.
  We need to solve these two equations to find the value of 'n'.
  From equation (1), we can rearrange it as follows:
  m x p + (n-m) x q = 9000
  m x p + n x q - m x q = 9000
  n x q - m x q = 9000 - m x p
  q x (n-m) = 9000 - m x p  ... (3)
  From equation (2), we know that:
  p x m < 3000 <= q x (n-m)
  m < 3000/p <= n-m
  m < 3 <= n-m  ... (4)
  Substituting equation (4) in equation (3), we get:
  q x 3 = 9000 - m x p
  q = (9000 - m x p) / 3
  Since 'q' is an integer, (9000 - m x p) must be divisible by 3.
  We can also say that m x p cannot be greater than $3000. The maximum value of 'm' can be 2. If we assume 'm' to be 1, then 'p' will be $3000. This means that 'n-m' will also be 2, and 'q' will be $3000. This satisfies both equations (1) and (2), and 'n' will be 3.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 3. 

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We need to find the number of members in the family.
  The median income is $3000.
  This means that half of the family members earn less than $3000, and the other half earn more than $3000.
  Let us assume there are 'n' members in the family.
  We need to find the value of 'n'.
  We know that the total income of the family is $9000.
  Therefore, the average income of each member is $9000/n.
  Since the median income is $3000, we know that there are n/2 members who earn less than $3000 and n/2 members who earn more than $3000.
  Let us assume that k members earn less than $3000.
  Therefore, n/2-k members earn more than $3000.
  Total income of the members who earn less than $3000 is k * $3000.
  Total income of the members who earn more than $3000 is (n/2-k) * $3000.
  Total income of the family per month is $9000.
  Therefore, k * $3000 + (n/2-k) * $3000 = $9000.
  Solving the above equation, we get k = n/4.
  Therefore, the number of members in the family is n = 4k = 4(n/4) = n.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 4.

Topic: Math
Question: A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join?
Choices:
  A: 2 months
  B: 4 months
  C: 23 months
  D: 24 months
  E: 84 months
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume C joined x months after B joined the business.
  The profit sharing ratio of A, B, and C is 4:6:12.
  Let's find the total profit shared by A and B first and then use that to find C's share.
  A's profit share = 4/22 * 375,000 = Rs.68,181.81
  B's profit share = 6/22 * 375,000 = Rs.102,272.73
  Total profit shared by A and B = 68,181.81 + 102,272.73 = Rs.170,454.54
  Now, we can find the time period for which C was in the business.
  C's profit share = 12/22 * 375,000 = Rs.204,545.45
  C's profit share - B's profit share = 204,545.45 - 102,272.73 = Rs.102,272.72
  Let's assume C was in the business for y months.
  Then, (120000 * y * 12)/12 * 22 = 102272.72
  Solving this equation, we get y = 23.
  Therefore, C joined the business 23 months after B.
  The answer is C: 23 months.
